20275 LVINLBVWd
20287 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
203c2 Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
20552 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
2060a GPIB status vector:
2061f status[0] - Device Clear State
2063e  status[1] - Device Trigger State
20660  status[2] - Listener Active State
20684 status[3] - Talker Active State
206a5 status[4] - Attention line asserted
206ca status[5] -
206d6 Controller In Charge
206eb  status[6] - Remote State
20705  status[7] - Lockout State
20721 status[8] - I/O Completed 
2073d status[9] - not used
20752  status[10]- not used
20768  status[11]- not used
2077f status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
207a7 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
207c7  status[14]- Timeout occured
207e4  status[15]- GPIB error detected
20808 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
2083d GPIB Error:
2084e -No error
2085d -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
20884 -No listeners detected on write
208a9 -Controller not addressed correctly
208d2 -Invalid argument(s)
208ed (perhaps bad address string????)
20913 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
20939 -I/O operation aborted
20955 -hardware not present
20970 -DMA error
20980 -DMA bus timeout
20996 -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
209bd progress
209cb -function not implemented
209ea -file system error
20a02 -shareable board exclusively owned
20a2a -GPIB bus error (commands)
20a4a -Serial Poll Byte Lost
20a66 -SRQ line cannot be cleared
20a87 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
20ae1 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.RNcount. The VI returns up to count data bytes from the device in data string. 
20c2f GPIB status vector:
20c44 status[0] - Device Clear State
20c63  status[1] - Device Trigger State
20c85  status[2] - Listener Active State
20ca9 status[3] - Talker Active State
20cca status[4] - Attention line asserted
20cef status[5] -
20cfb Controller In Charge
20d10  status[6] - Remote State
20d2a  status[7] - Lockout State
20d46 status[8] - I/O Completed 
20d62 status[9] - not used
20d77  status[10]- not used
20d8d  status[11]- not used
20da4 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
20dcc status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
20dec  status[14]- Timeout occured
20e09  status[15]- GPIB error detectedA=data string contains count data bytes from the GPIB device.

2ecd1 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
2ed2d status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
2ede5 GPIB status vector:
2edfa status[0] - Device Clear State
2ee19  status[1] - Device Trigger State
2ee3b  status[2] - Listener Active State
2ee5f status[3] - Talker Active State
2ee80 status[4] - Attention line asserted
2eea5 status[5] -
2eeb1 Controller In Charge
2eec6  status[6] - Remote State
2eee0  status[7] - Lockout State
2eefc status[8] - I/O Completed 
2ef18 status[9] - not used
2ef2d  status[10]- not used
2ef43  status[11]- not used
2ef5a status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
2ef82 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
2efa2  status[14]- Timeout occured
2efbf  status[15]- GPIB error detected
2efe1 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
2f0de 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
2f214 The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
2f285   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
2f2b5  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
2f2e4  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device.

492a3      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.

6e029 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
6e12b      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
6e15e      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
6e18d      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
6e1c7      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
6e200      error, and a positive value is a warning.
6e230      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
6e25f      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
6e290 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
6e2ec (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
6e445      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
6e479      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
6e4b3      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
6e4ec      error, and a positive value is a warning.
6e51c      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
6e54e      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

75ab4 LVINLBVWgH
75ac6 /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
75bfa Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
75d0e VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
75e67 True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

80ab5 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
80bb1 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
80d0a      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
80d3e      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
80d78      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
80db1      error, and a positive value is a warning.
80de1      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
80e13      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
80e44 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

810ae f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters:

9bd22 Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.$

a5a48 (I32) 
a5a4f A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
a5b4b (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
a5ca4      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
a5cd8      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
a5d12      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
a5d4b      error, and a positive value is a warning.
a5d7b      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
a5dad      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
a5dde [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

a5e88 (ABC) 
a5e8f The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
a5f46 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
a6048      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
a607b      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
a60aa      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
a60e4      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
a611d      error, and a positive value is a warning.
a614d      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
a617c      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
a61ad ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

c06d7 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
c0830      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
c0864      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
c089e      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
c08d7      error, and a positive value is a warning.
c0907      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
c0939      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
c096a [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
c09f6 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
c0adc GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
c0b0b VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
c0b2a GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
c0b64 Optional Parameter Default Values:
c0b87     bd - GPIB board (0)
c0b9f     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
c0bc8     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
c0bf5     logical addr - VXI logical address 
c0c1e EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.
c0c80 INSTR{GPIB::5}"

c0d75 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
c0e70 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters:

e593d When you use the serial port VIs on a Sun SPARCstation, the port number parameter is 0 for /dev/ttya, 1 for /dev/ttyb, and so on.
e59bf On the Macintosh, port 0 is the modem, using the drivers .ain and .aout. Port 1 is the printer, using the drivers.bin and .bout. To get more ports on a Macintosh, you must install other boards, with the accompanying drivers.

e92f0 Wrequested byte count specifies the number of characters to be read. f1345 error out is a cluster that describes the error status after this VI executes. If an error occurred before this VI was called, error out is the same as error in. Otherwise, error out shows the error, if any, that occurred in this VI. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
f1547 status is TRUE if an error occurred, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code."

fedc4 LVINLBVW
fedd6 |error in is a cluster that describes the error status before this VI executes. If error in indicates that an error occurred before this VI was called, this VI may choose not to execute its function, but just pass the error through to its error out cluster. If no error has occurred, then this VI executes normally and sets its own error status in error out. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
ff055 status is TRUE if an error occurred before this VI was called, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code."
ff111 no error
ff11a ERROR
ff120 no error
ff129 ERROR
ff132 code is the number identifying an error or warning. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code. Use the error handler VIs to look up the meaning of this code and to display the corresponding error message.
ff23f source is a string that indicates the origin of the error, if any. Usually source is the name of the VI in which the error occurred.
ff2c6 error out is a cluster that describes the error status after this VI executes. If an error occurred before this VI was called, error out is the same as error in. Otherwise, error out shows the error, if any, that occurred in this VI. Use the error handler VIs to look up the error code and to display the corresponding error message. Using error in and error out clusters is a convenient way to check errors and to specify execution order by wiring the error output from one subVI to the error input of the next.
ff4c8 status is TRUE if an error occurred, or FALSE if not. If status is TRUE, code is a non-zero error code. If status is FALSE, code can be zero or a warning code."

132a03 DIO Port Write.vi
133709 ?~<>
1338a5 ?>&>&fffffffffffffffffffffffffffffffffff~dfFffffdfffffffffffffffffffffff
1339cc wwww
133b83 7UUUU
133e90 RSRC
133e97 LVINLBVW
133ea6 84(u32) task ID: identifies the group and I/O pattern.D@(u32) pattern: specifies the new state of the lines in the port.
133f21 x(i32) line mask: determines which lines in the port the write affects. If you set line mask to -1, the VI writes to the entire port and sets all the lines in the port to the states specified by the bits in pattern. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI changes only line n in the port to the state that bit n of pattern specifies. The default setting for line mask is -1.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.
1340d1 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram. 13a82d (i32) line mask: determines which lines this VI reads. If you set line mask to -1 (all ones), the VI reads the entire port. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI reads only line n of the port. If the state of line n is high, the VI sets bit n of pattern. The VI sets to 0 the bits of pattern that correspond to lines the VI has not read. The default setting for line mask is -1 which is shown as all ones since the binary representation is the default selection.62(u32) pattern: the data the VI read from the port.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.

141770 (gc(i16) device: the device number you assigned to the data acquisition device when you configured it.
1417d9 /(i16) port width: the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4-bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8.
14187e When port width is greater than the physical port width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port  number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5.
141a0c ?(i32) line direction map: specifies the direction of each line in the port. If a bit is 0 in the line map, the line is an input line. If a bit is 1, the line is an output line. Setting line direction map to -1 makes all the lines in a port output lines. Setting line direction map to 0 makes all the lines in a port input lines. Except for the NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10, this is how you must use line direction map. The NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10 are the only boards on which you can configure lines within a port for different directions. The default for line direction map is 0.
141c4e (u32) task ID: uniquely identifies the group. You use this value as the task ID to refer to this group in subsequent digital port VI calls.
141cdd (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
141da5      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
141dd9      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
141e13      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
141e4d      error, and a positive value is a warning.
141e7d      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
141eaf      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
141ee0 xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
141f59 D(string) port number: specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use an SCXI-1160, SCXI-1161, SCXI-1162, or SCXI-1163 module, use the SCx!MDy syntax, where x is the chassis and y is the module device number, to specify the module."
1420a1 no error

1420b0 no error
1420b9 ERROR
1420c0 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
1421b0 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
142309      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
14233d      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.

14d3cb HDcode out is the error code indicated by the error in or error code.
14d414 no error
14d41d ERROR
14d423 no error
14d42c ERROR
14d434 =type of dialog determines what type dialog box will be displayed, if any. Regardless of its value, the VI outputs error information and message describing the error.
14d4df displays no dialog box. This is useful if you want to have programmatic control over how the error is handled.
14d552 (the default value) displays a dialog box with a single OK button. After the user responds, the VI returns control to the main VI.
14d5d9 displays a dialog box with buttons allowing the user to either continue or stop. If the user cancels, the VI calls the Stop function to halt execution. 
14d675 no dialog
14d67f OK message
14d68a continue or stop message
14d6a6 exception action is a way for you to create exceptions to error handling. You can treat what is normally an error as no error, or treat a no error condition as an error using this parameter. 
14d76a (the default value) performs no error exception handling. 
14d7a9 cancels error under the following conditions:
14d7d9 If the VI detects an error, as described in the status and error code parameters, and if that error code value matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to FALSE, code out to 0, and source out to an empty string. An empty exception source string matches any error source string.
14d92d sets error under the following conditions:
14d95a If the VI detects no error, as described in the status and error code parameters, but the code value of error in matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to TRUE, code out to the code value from error in, and source out to the source value from error in.
14da93 b^exception code is the error code that you want to treat as an exception. By default, it is 0.
14daf5 error code is a numeric error code. If error in indicates an error, the VI ignores error code. If not, the VI tests it. A non-zero value signifies an error.
14db94 no exception
14dba2 cancel error on match
14dbb8 set error on match
14dbcc user-defined codes is an array of the numeric error codes you define in your VIs. The VI searches this array after searching the internal list of error codes. Codes in the range of 5000 to 9999 are reserved for users.
14dca8 user-defined descriptions is an array of descriptions of user-defined codes. If an incoming error matches one in user-defined codes, the VI uses the corresponding description from user-defined descriptions in message.
14dd82 2.source out indicates the source of the error.
14ddb2 }yexception source is the error message that you want to use to test for an exception. By default, it is an empty string. 
14de2f error source is an optional string you can use to describe the source of error code. The VI uses the string in message if there is an error.
14debc jferror in describes an error that you want to check. If unwired, this VI checks error code for errors.
14df26 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
14dfd7 no error

14e029 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
14e0c2 |xerror out contains the same information as status out, code out, and source out. It has the same structure as error in.
14e13e status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.

15a223 Code
15a228 error codes (hidden)
15a373 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

15abd1 GetCommErr
15abf4 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.SD
15aea0 message
15af1b  INSTRUCTIONS:
15af2b Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
15b223 Other Uses:
15b231 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
15b3ad user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
15b4ae exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  H

15bfdb QDSP NumBytesGTZero:  The number of bytes to allocate should be greater than zero.SDSP InvalidDataType:  The data type can only be 4 bytes long(0) or 2 bytes long(1).
15c082 DSP IndexSizeOffsetErr:  The size+offset should be less than or equal to the size of the DSP Handle Structure which you index into.[DSP IndexSizeGTZero:  The size of the New DSP Handle Structure should be greater than zero.FDSP OffsetGEZero:  The offset should be greater than or equal to zero.KDSP CopyNumGTZero:  The number of data to copy should be greater than zero.uDSP Invalid CopyType:  The entire/partial copy selector can only select between entire copy (0) and partial copy (1).GDSP PathnameTooLong:  The path name should be less than 256 characters.
15c2b3 DSP InvalidArrayType:  The array type can only be 32-bit floating point data(0), 16-bit long integer data(1) or 32-bit short integer data(2).:DSP AllocArrayFailed:  Failed to allocate a LabVIEW array.2DSP SourceNumErr:  You can only select one source.bDSP InvalidBytesSelect:  bytes/element selector can only select between 4 bytes(0) and 2 bytes(1).nDSP ErrInGetFunctionHandle:  An error occurred when calling the function GetIndirectFunctionHandle in the CIN.TDSP LoadDLLLibErr:  An error occurred when loading a function in dsp.dll in the CIN.MDSP NotFindFunctionInDLL:  An error occurred when loading dsp.dll in the CIN.
15c524 DSP GROUP_ERR.  The function ID specified does not belong to any group that is part of the DSP Library currently running on the board.
15c5ab DSP FNC_ERR:  The function ID specified does not correspond to a function that is part of the DSP Library currently running on the board.
15c635 DSP NoBrdRespToTransfer:  The DSP board on which you are trying to load the COFF file is not responding to the transfer of the file.  Check if there is a board in the slot desired and verify with the DAQCONF utility.
15c70e DSP AddrSpaceErr:  The COFF file you are trying to load is linked with a memory map that exceeds the maximum memory space allowed by the WE DSP32C chip (2^24).GDSP CoffSectErr:  Found an unimplemented section flag in the COFF file.
15c7f6 DSP CoffHdrErr:  The file you are attempting to load to the DSP board is not created using the WE DSP32C tools (not an acceptable COFF file).gDSP COFF_FilePathErr:  Could not find the DSP Library file in the directory set by the DAQCONF utility.dDSP TimeOutErr:  The Kernel did not respond or finish function execution in the selected time limit.GDSP HandleAllocErr:  Failed to allocate a handle in the interface code.pDSP HandleSlotErr:  The DSP Handle used does not belong to the same board on which the function request is made.vDSP NotDSPHandle:  The DSP Handle specified is not valid for this board:  it has either been freed or never allocated.tDSP TransferSizeErr:  The size of requested block transfer does not have enough space allocated for it on the board.bDSP ParamSizeErr:  One of the parameters does not have enough space allocated for it on the board.PDSP PtrNotFound:  The DSP address pointer could not be found to free the buffer.
15cbaa DSP TooManyAllocs:  The Memory Look Up Table is full:  no more allocations allowed before freeing up some DSP handles (maximum allowed = 128).wDSP HandleNotFound:  The DSP Handle specified is not found on this board:  it has either been freed or never allocated.iDSP TooBigAnOffset:  The indexing requested falls outside of the buffer into which indexing is requested.FDSP ZERO_ALLOCATION:  There are no allocated buffers on the DSP board.
15cd62 DSP MEM_HARDWARE_ERR:  The onboard hardware diagnostic software found a memory hardware error.  Running functions on the board is unreliable.fDSP NotPowerOfTwo:  The size of the input array must be a valid power of two:  size = 2^m, 0 < m < 14.HDSP RankErr:  The rank of the filter must meet:  1 <= (2rank+1) <= size.ODSP LenGEOne:  The number of coefficients must be greater than or equal to one.XDSP FilterDesignErr:  The filter cannot be designed with the specified input parameters.lDSP LeakErr:  The leakage coefficient, Leak, must meet:  0 <= Leak <= u, where u is the step-size parameter.FDSP StepSizeErr:  The step-size parameter u must meet:  0 <= u <= 0.1.NDSP AttenGTRipple:  The attenuation must be greater than the ripple amplitude.NDSP NullVectorErr:  The input vector is null. 16652d  INSTRUCTIONS:
16653d Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
166835 Other Uses:
166843 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
1669bf user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
166ac0 exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  
166cf7 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.

167f00 General Error Handler.vi
167f1f 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.

169672 ,yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
1696ed &port width is the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
16978d When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
169916 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data to write to the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit for the port specified by the port number control. 
1699b0 M(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for output and then writes the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply writes the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
169b01 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

16e4c8 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
16e57b The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
16e5d6 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
16e6c0 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
16e748 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.

16fcab dyudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
16fd26 =port width is the total width in bits or the number of lines of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
16fddd When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
16ff66 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data read from the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit from the port specified by the port number control. 
16ffff J(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for input and then reads the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply reads the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
17014d )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

1effb7 1) Plug in and turn on LC103 Mainboard test box.

1f001a     Mainboard tester (#74C216-1).
1f003c 3) Connect Fluke 8840A to DVM plugs on front panel of test box.

1f00fe 6) Press ENTER when ready, choose test to perform and press START.H

1f2bcb                                      Setup Procedure:
1f2c02 1) Plug in and turn on LC103 Mainboard test box.
1f2c33 2) Attach power adapter and RS-232 cable to LC103
1f2c65     Mainboard tester (#74C216-1).
1f2c87 3) Connect Fluke 8840A to DVM plugs on front panel of test box.
1f2cc7 4) Connect Lo Capacity leads to UUT plugs on front of test box.
1f2d07 5) Connect 50 pin ribbon cable from PC to right side of test box.
1f2d49 6) Press ENTER when ready, choose test to perform and press START.
